Appendices                                                                                                                                                           Chapter 10
Appendix 3 -2nd Interaction with Case studies Interview 
Structure 
Interview guideline for case studies in the thesis project 
”Domestication of Technology: Innovations making sense within 
communities” 
Researcher: Martha Cecilia Fernandez Contreras 
Technical University of Denmark 
Contact: ceciliafdz.94@gmail.com  
This interview guideline has three parts:  
• Demographics of Startup - These questions attempt to understand the foundation of the startup and the 
internal activities  
• Use of methods and reﬂection - These questions focus in the understanding of application of methods in daily 
activities 
• Personal, good and bad, experiences with methods and reﬂection - These questions attempt to understand 
the reﬂection process of using speciﬁc design methods 
Demographics of Startup 
• Can you tell me about your project? 
• How and why did the project start? 
• What is your mission and vision?  
• Where are you located and who are you targeting? 
• What are the main roles in operations? 
• Do you work in teams or individual tasks? 
• How do you manage the communication within the team? 
• From which nationalities and study lines is each member of the team? 
• How do you think this has affected the team dynamic? 
Use of methods and reﬂection  
• I saw that you were part of ____, ____ and ____. What was the biggest learning along this experiences? 
•  Do you remember some tools from those experiences that you have taken into your activities or 
mindset? 
• I saw that you have use ____, ____ and ____. How have you applied it in the daily activities of the Startups? 
• How do you make a strategy for developing or improving a prototype? 
• I saw that you have done _________ and __________ to get insights about your customer or user, can you tell 
me more about this?  
• How did you decide the approach 
• How long did it took? 
• Did you involve a third party? 
• How did you make it possible 
• Which hard and soft skills do you consider fundamental for developing a product? 
Personal, good and bad, experiences with methods and reﬂection 
• Do you think these methods have helped or limited you in any way? 
• What has been the biggest insight about this process, what is a key task you have found is fundamental for 
this process? 
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities

ahí, a través de Lucas, yo he aprendido mucho a mediar, a hablar el idioma político en idioma más, más humano y 
menos técnico, menos ingenieril. Y al mismo tiempo hemos aprendido también, digamos a veces, limitarnos, porque 
luego Lucas, cuando vende algo, lo vende con sus palabras. Pero tecnológicamente también se vuelve un reto crearlo. 
No quieres ser como un bacán, fuerte, interesante, que hemos ido puliendo en la dinámica. Somos o ya hemos 
funcionado muy bien, como una mancuerna de traducción de lo ingenieril a lo digital o digestiva, digerible y al mismo 
tiempo, pues hablar técnico si se necesita.

Appendix 11 - Concept Catalogue 
Concept 1 
The concept aims to show how the iterative process happens between validating with the customer 
and working inside the company. With a pivoting movement the model intends to illustrates the 
relationship between user validation testing and improvements done by the startup. It was considered 
that the arrow can have as many pivoting as necessary, as long as it keeps going forward resulting in 
a positive outcome.  
 
The difference that matters 
In product development, user validation is fundamental. Having a model that allows to document each 
step of the process gives the startup the chance to understand their whole journey.  
This concept is relatively easy to implement as it is seeing more as a document tool that makes visual 
the outcomes of each step in the product development process. Startups will have the complete 
information and everyone in the team can look at it and understand what is the next step to take.  
Strengths
Weaknesses
• Documents every step of the process
• Depends on the user on the amount and detail 
of information they decide to document.
• Easy to understand what was the 
outcome in each step and with which 
actor (startup or user)
• Might become to crowded 
• Need to deﬁne key words 
• Everyone can assume diﬀerent things from the 
same information if its not well explained
• Easy to be applied
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities 
 
125
==PAGE:127==
Appendices                                                                                                                                                           Chapter 10
Concept 2 
This concept looks to show the relation between decisions done by startups, users and stakeholders. 
The arrows in the model looks to symbolise a dynamic system behaviour between the three agents 
and how does each other affect between them. It was considered that the proportions of the model 
could vary depending on the power level in the ecosystem in a way to make visible who is the 
stakeholder that should be considered for a decision.  
 
The difference that matters 
In a startup ecosystem understanding how each stakeholder affects the other is crucial. It was 
understood by the hyper-collaboration and startup ecosystem analysis the potential of working 
together and improving the product development process in a startup.  
The dynamic of the system is visualised and the model can vary in different times. Over time the 
startup will have a documented map of the power inﬂuence. 
Strengths
Weaknesses
• Shows the dynamic system behaviour
• It might be perceived as complex and too 
general to give concrete information
• Complete overview of the inﬂuence power
• Factors to decide the stakeholder power will 
need to be deﬁned
• Allows to take decisions based on the 
stakeholders power
• Decisions might be taken based on 
assumption rather than concrete information
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities 
 
126
==PAGE:128==
Appendices                                                                                                                                                           Chapter 10
Concept 3  
Concept three aims to create a “radiography” on the relation between a product features and 
adoption factors. It is considered that if a product ﬁts most of all the adoption factors this will be 
accepted in an emerging market easily. By detailing the product functions the startup is aware of the 
value that they perceive they are giving to the user. If each of the functions has a reason to ﬁll each 
adoption factor it will be easier for the startup to understand the opportunities or risks they are facing.  
 
The difference that matters 
This concept proposes a radiography between the technical part and the human part of a product. By 
acknowledging this startups can be aware of the needs to improve the product and enter the market 
in an easier form. 
It is considered that this concept relatively easy to implement as it doesn’t require a lot of time to get 
ﬁll and it can be modifying along time.  
When using color code post its to write each relation, startups can identify opportunities or risks in a 
near future.  
Strengths
Weaknesses
• Shows a relation between product features 
and adoption factors
• Needs key questions to answer each factor
• Identiﬁes opportunities and risks before user 
validation or market entrance
• Requires a reﬂection after ﬁlling the tool to 
understand the outcomes of the information.
• Has the possibility to be modiﬁed at any point
• Provides information to diﬀerent departments 
of the startup (product development, sales, 
marketing, etc.)
• Can be modiﬁed by a single person or a team
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities

Appendices                                                                                                                                                           Chapter 10
Appendix 12 - Concept Evaluation 
Concept 1 
With concept one it was considered that the following dimensions will be impacted: 
• Strategy, the model will allow the startup to create a plan to achieve their mission and vision. 
• Need, this concept proposes a relation between customers and the products attributes.  
• User, customer, this concept shows how the user behaviour and responses to the product 
changes the development process. 
• Technology, the concept relates the user behaviour into the product principles. 
 
Product’s raison d’être: 
Possible 
    + With an iterative tool is easy for the startups to use it in their daily activities. 
    - Each startup will have a different way to use it (e.g. teams, individual, whole company) 
Profitable 
    + Documents information for possible investors. 
    - Requires time to document all the information, hours of work will have to be invested in the 
model. 
Desirable 
    + The outcomes makes easier for the startups to document and look at their process. 
    - Some startups might consider it as not needed in their operations. 
Sensible 
    + The concept gives the startup a visual aid of their development process.  
- It is needed to deﬁne the criteria of how to deﬁne power in the model 
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities

Concept 2 
With concept two it was considered that the following dimensions will be impacted: 
• Need, one of the parts of the concept involves the understanding of the customers problems and 
how does this affect the startup ecosystem. 
• User, customer, the concept considers the user behaviour and response to the decisions made by 
the startups ecosystem 
• Technology, concept 2 involves the production agents, who are considered part of the 
stakeholders in the ecosystem. 
 
Product’s raison d’être: 
Possible 
    + All startups are aware of the basic stakeholders in their ecosystem so they can create the model 
    - Each startup will have a different perspective of power of each stakeholder in the ecosystem. 
Profitable 
    + Allows identify power stakeholders who could invest in the company. 
    - It will require time to draft the ﬁrst version of the canvas, taking the time of other tasks.  
Desirable 
    + The outcomes gives the startup a panorama for potential collaborations. 
    - Some startups might feel is not needed at a certain point of their development. 
Sensible 
    + The product beneﬁts the user by providing an overview of the dynamic system behaviour they 
pertain.  
-The concept might be too complicate and need to make it more accesible. 
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities 
 
129
==PAGE:131==
Appendices                                                                                                                                                           Chapter 10
Concept 3 
With concept three it was considered that the following dimensions will be impacted: 
• Strategy, the model will allow the startup to create a plan to achieve their mission and vision while 
having a balance between user and company. 
• Need, this concept proposes a relation between customers and the products attributes.  
• User, customer, this concept shows the relation between the adoption factors that are relevant for 
the user and customer in order to accept the product. 
• Goal specification, by applying this concept the properties and performance of the product is 
validated before user testing. 
• Product, the form and appearance of a product, as well as the technical solutions are correlated to 
the adoption factors. 
• Technology, the product principles are outlined and detailed in a technical and user perception. 
 
Product’s raison d’être: 
Possible 
    + With an iterative tool is feasible to adopt it in the startups' scenarios 
    - Each startup will have a different way to use it (e.g. teams, individual, whole company) 
Proﬁtable 
    + Reduces the workforce creating bigger opportunities to improve current solutions. 
    - It will require time to draft the ﬁrst version of the canvas, taking the time of other tasks.  
Desirable 
    + The outcomes makes it more appealing compared to current solutions. 
    - Some startups might consider it as not needed in their operations. 
Sensible 
    + The product beneﬁts the end-user and the customer by improving current solutions  
- The product has to be improved in graphical design to make it more attractive.

==PAGE:133==
Appendices                                                                                                                                                           Chapter 10
Perceived Value Questionnaire guideline for case studies in the thesis project  
”Domestication of Technology: Innovations making sense within 
communities” 
Researcher: Martha Cecilia Fernandez Contreras 
Technical University of Denmark 
Contact: ceciliafdz.94@gmail.com  
This interview guideline has three parts: 
• Action - These questions attempt to identify the feelings connected to the model, and if those draw 
them closer or pull them away. 
• Barriers - These questions focus on how users internalise and understand the tool. 
• Motivation - These questions answer how positive or negative the user perception has been with the 
tool. 
Action 
• Scale question: On a scale of 1-10, how easy was to understand the tool? 
• Scale question: On a scale of 1-10, how comfortable will you feel using the tool? 
• Open-ended question: Which three words would you use to describe the tool? 
Barriers 
• Open-ended question: Please share a few things that can be improved in the tool. 
• Open-ended question: In your perception, what is the biggest challenge to use this tool? 
• Open-ended question: In your perception, will this tool provide meaningful information to the 
Startup? 
Motivation 
• Scale question: On a scale of 1-10, how likely are you to use it in your Startup? 
• Scale question: On a scale of 1-10, how likely are you to recommend to a friend or colleague? 
• Open-ended question: Why would you use it in your daily operations? 
• Open-ended question: Please share a few things that you liked about the tool. 
Domesticating technology: Innovations making sense within communities
